## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling / solid mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship in materials, where stress depends on strain through constitutive laws (elastic, plastic, or viscoplastic) and temperature modulates material properties like elastic modulus, yield strength, and hardening behavior.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke's law (temperature-dependent): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elasticity at fixed T)
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (linear modulus variation with temperature)
- Exponential thermal softening of modulus: sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * epsilon (thermally activated modulus decay)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (Ramberg-Osgood type plastic hardening)
- Hollomon equation with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (power-law hardening with thermal effects)
- Johnson-Cook type model: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 + c3 * T) (strain hardening with linear thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 - c2 * T**c3) (power-law hardening with homologous temperature effect)
- Ludwik equation: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Voce hardening: sigma = c0 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon) (exponential saturation hardening)
- Voce with thermal dependence: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (1 - exp(c2 * epsilon)) (saturating hardening with temperature-dependent saturation stress)
- Swift law: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 (power-law with pre-strain offset)
- Polynomial stress-strain: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (nonlinear elastic or early plastic regime)
- Hyperbolic tangent hardening: sigma = c0 * tanh(c1 * epsilon) * (1 + c2 * T) (saturating stress with temperature modulation)
- Zerilli-Armstrong BCC type: sigma = c0 + c1 * exp((c2 + c3 * epsilon) * T) (thermally activated dislocation glide model)
- Arrhenius-type flow stress: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) * T**c3 (high-temperature deformation with thermal activation)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Temperature-dependent modulus → multiplicative factor on strain: (c0 + c1*T)*epsilon or c0*exp(c1*T)*epsilon
- Strain hardening saturation → (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) or tanh(c*epsilon) forms indicating dislocation density saturation
- Power-law strain hardening → epsilon**c with 0 < c < 1 reflecting work hardening in metals (typically c ~ 0.1-0.5)
- Thermal softening → (1 - c*T**m) multiplicative factor or exponential decay exp(-c*T) reflecting reduced dislocation barriers
- Yield stress offset → additive constant c0 + f(epsilon) separating elastic limit from hardening contribution
- Coupled strain-temperature interaction → products like epsilon**c1 * T**c2 or epsilon * exp(c*T) reflecting thermally activated plasticity
- Pre-strain or initial condition offset → (epsilon + c)**n instead of epsilon**n to handle non-zero initial conditions
- Competing hardening and softening → difference of terms like c0*epsilon**c1 - c2*T reflecting dynamic recovery at high temperature

The GT has these basis functions in terms of (T, epsilon):

4. constant
5. `T*log(epsilon+1)`

Now I need to check each candidate to see if it can represent exactly this combination of basis functions.

Let me systematically check candidates that look promising - those with `log` terms involving `epsilon` and linear terms in `T` and `epsilon`.

Now let me reconsider the GT structure. Perhaps I can rewrite it differently.

GT = `T*(-0.9443*epsilon - 0.4785 + 8.062*log(epsilon+1)) + 429.36*epsilon + 168.57 - 2839.3*log(epsilon+1)`

So GT = `T*f(epsilon) + g(epsilon)` where:
- `f(epsilon) = -0.9443*epsilon - 0.4785 + 8.062*log(epsilon+1)`
- `g(epsilon) = 429.36*epsilon + 168.57 - 2839.3*log(epsilon+1)`

Note that `g(epsilon) ≈ 352.18 * f(epsilon)` would require checking:
`352.18*(-0.9443*epsilon - 0.4785 + 8.062*log(epsilon+1))` = `-332.5*epsilon - 168.5 + 2839*log(epsilon+1)`

But g = `429.36*epsilon + 168.57 - 2839.3*log(epsilon+1)` = `-(-429.36*epsilon - 168.57 + 2839.3*log(epsilon+1))`

So g ≈ -352.18*f? Let's check: `-352.18*f = 352.18*0.9443*epsilon + 352.18*0.4785 - 352.18*8.062*log(epsilon+1)` = `332.6*epsilon + 168.6 - 2839.3*log(epsilon+1)`

But g = `429.36*epsilon + 168.57 - 2839.3*log(epsilon+1)`. The constant and log coefficients match but the epsilon coefficient doesn't (332.6 vs 429.36). So g ≠ -352.18*f. The difference is `(429.36-332.6)*epsilon = 96.76*epsilon ≈ c0*epsilon`.

So GT = `T*f(epsilon) + (-352.18)*f(epsilon) + 96.83*epsilon` = `(T-352.18)*f(epsilon) + 96.83*epsilon`
= `(T-352.18)*(-0.9443*epsilon - 0.4785 + 8.062*log(epsilon+1)) + 96.83*epsilon`

This confirms the original form. The key point: GT is linear in T with coefficients that are functions of epsilon involving `{epsilon, 1, log(epsilon+1)}`.

For candidates with `T/(c1+epsilon)`: this gives `T/(c1+epsilon)` which is a rational function of epsilon times T. This is NOT `T*log(epsilon+1)`. These are fundamentally different functions.

- Only Candidate 45 has `T^c2 * log(epsilon)` type term.

- Candidate 59 has `epsilon^c7 * log(epsilon+1)` without T.

None of the candidates can produce both `T*log(epsilon+1)` AND `log(epsilon+1)` as separate basis functions.
